The authors also would like to thank the Census Bureau field representatives and telephone interviewers who conducted the interviews that provide the data in this report. Without their dedication, the preparation of this report or any report from the Current Population Survey would be impossible.

### iv

### [INTRODUCTION](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf)

The U.S. Census Bureau pro - duces annual poverty estimates [to measure the economic well-](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [being of households, families, and](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) individuals in the United States. [This report provides estimates](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [of two measures of poverty: the](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [official poverty measure and the](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [Supplemental Poverty Measure](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [(SPM). The official poverty mea](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) - sure, produced since the 1960s, defines poverty by comparing pretax money income to a national poverty threshold adjusted by

[,](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html)

family composition. The official poverty measure is used as an input to determine eligibility for several government programs and has been used as a benchmark of economic well-being since its adoption.

[The SPM, produced in collabora](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) - [tion with the Bureau of Labor](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) Statistics (BLS), extends the offi - cial poverty measure by account - [ing for several government pro](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [-](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [grams that are designed to assist](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [low-income families but are not](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [included in official poverty mea](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) - sure calculations. The SPM also accounts for geographic varia [-](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) tion in housing expenses when calculating poverty thresholds and includes federal and state [taxes, work expenses, and medi](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) - [cal expenses. The SPM has been](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) released annually since 2011, with estimates going back to 2009. It does not replace the official pov - erty measure, but rather provides [a different metric of economic](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [well-being that includes resources](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html)

#### [Background](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833)

The Census Bureau has pro - [duced poverty estimates since](http://www.census.gov/) [the 1960s. Following the Office of](http://www.bls.gov/cex/pumd-getting-started-guide.htm) [Management and Budget’s (OMB)](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty.html) [Statistical Policy Directive 14, the](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [official poverty measure classi](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) [-](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) fies families and individuals as in poverty if their pretax money income falls below a threshold [adjusted by family composition.](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) Poverty thresholds are adjusted annually for inflation using the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers (CPI-U). The official

#### Official Poverty Measure

#### [Measurement units](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) Families (individuals related by birth, marriage, or adoption) or unrelated [individuals.](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html)

#### [Poverty threshold](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) Three times the cost of a minimum food diet in 1963.

#### Threshold Vary by family size, composition, and adjustments age of householder.

#### Updating thresholds Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers: all items.

#### [Resource measure](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) Gross pretax cash income.

#### [Universe](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) Civilian noninstitutionalized population, excluding unrelated individuals under the age of 15 for whom poverty status cannot be determined.

#### Time series 1959–present.

#### DIFFERENCES IN POVERTY MEASURES

#### [Supplemental Poverty Measure](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

[Resource units (official family definition plus any](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) coresident unrelated children, foster children, and unmarried partners and their relatives) or unrelated individuals (who are not otherwise included in the family definition).

#### Based on recent expenditures for food, clothing, [shelter, utilities, telephone, and internet](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/technical-documentation/subject-definitions.html) (FCSUti).

#### Vary by family size, composition, and housing tenure with geographic adjustments for differences in housing costs.

#### Most recent 5-year moving average of [expenditures on FCSUti, lagged 1 year.](http://www.census.gov/newsroom/blogs/research-matters/2024/09/administrative-data-nonresponse-bias-cps-asec.html)

Cash income, plus noncash benefits that [resource units can use to meet their FCSUti](http://www.census.gov/newsroom/blogs/research-matters/2024/09/administrative-data-nonresponse-bias-cps-asec.html) [needs, minus taxes (or plus tax credits), work](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2023/demo/SEHSD-WP2023-02.html) [expenses, medical expenses, and child support](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2023/demo/SEHSD-WP2023-02.html) paid to another household.

#### [Official poverty measure universe, plus unrelated](https://www.nber.org/research/business-cycle-dating) [individuals under the age of 15.](https://www.nber.org/research/business-cycle-dating)

#### Sex and Age

The official poverty rate for women fell 0.5 percentage points to 11.9 [percent in 2023 but remained](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [higher than the rate for men (10.2](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [percent). The poverty rate for men](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [was not statistically different from](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [2022 (Figure 2 and Table A-1).](http://www.bls.gov/cex/pumd-getting-started-guide.htm)

[Among the age groups in Figure](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [2, only 18- to 64-year-olds expe](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) - rienced a significant change in poverty between 2022 and 2023, declining 0.6 percentage points to 10.0 percent in 2023. People under [18 years old had a higher pov](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) [-](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) erty rate (15.3 percent) than both 18- to 64-year-olds (10.0 percent) and those 65 years and older (9.7 percent).

#### Type of Unit

[Official poverty rates did not](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [change significantly for people](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) in families, regardless of family [type (Figure 2 and Table A-2).](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [Of people in families, those in](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [married-couple families had the](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [lowest poverty rate (5.2 percent),](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) [while those in female-householder](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) families had the highest (23.6 percent).

#### [Poverty rates for unrelated individ](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) - [uals decreased by 0.9 percentage](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) points between 2022 and 2023 to [19.2 percent.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

### [Percent](http://www.census.gov/newsroom/blogs/research-matters/2024/09/administrative-data-nonresponse-bias-cps-asec.html)

[As the SPM demonstrates, these](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [factors can have a significant effect](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [on poverty rates. The rest of this](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [report explores poverty using the](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [SPM. The SPM provides an addi](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [-](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) tional perspective on economic well-being by expanding the defini - tion of official poverty to include [noncash benefits, account for](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [income and payroll taxes, subtract](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) other necessary expenses, use a [more inclusive resource sharing](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [unit, and account for geographic](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [differences in housing costs.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

#### [The remainder of this report uses](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) [official](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html)

[+](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html)

#### [when drawing comparisons](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) between the SPM and the official poverty measure. Official

+

denotes the official poverty measure using [the same universe as the SPM,](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) which includes unrelated individu - als under the age of 15. Using offi - cial

+

#### allows for direct comparisons of the two concepts with the same reference universe.

#### SPM by Selected Characteristics

[In 2023, the overall SPM rate was](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) 12.9 percent, 0.5 percentage points [higher than in 2022. This was](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [the second consecutive annual](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [increase in the SPM rate (Table](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [B-2).](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html)

[Figure 4 presents annual SPM rates](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) for 2022 and 2023 across a set of demographic characteristics. Estimates for additional demo - graphic groups are available in [Table B-3.](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html)

#### [Sex and Age](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

SPM rates increased by 0.5 per - centage points for both men and women in 2023. The SPM rate [for women (13.4 percent) was](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [higher than the rate for men (12.4](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) percent).

#### In 2023, the SPM rate increased 1.3 [percentage points for those under](https://data.census.gov/) 18 years old to 13.7 percent. SPM rates for both 18- to 64-year-olds

### Official 65+

[](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html)   [](https://stats.bls.gov/pir/spmhome.htm) [](https://stats.bls.gov/pir/spmhome.htm)         [+ ](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html)

[Note: Official](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) includes unrelated individuals under age 15. Population as of March of the following year. The Supplemental Poverty Measure (SPM) estimates for 2019 and beyond reflect the implementation of revised SPM methodology. More information is available in the SPM technical documenation at <[https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)>. The data for 2017 and beyond reflect the implementation of an updated processing system. The data for 2013 and beyond reflect the implementation of the redesigned income questions. Refer to Table B-2 for historical footnotes. The data points are placed at the midpoints of the respective years. More information on recessions is available in Appendix C. More information on confidentiality protection, sampling error, nonsampling error, and definitions is available at <[https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf)>. Source: U.S. Census Bureau, Current Population Survey, 2010 to 2024 Annual Social and Economic Supplements (CPS ASEC).

### [DISTRIBUTION OF PEOPLE](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [BY INCOME-TO-POVERTY](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [RATIOS: 2023](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html)

The methodological differences between the official poverty measure and the SPM not only result in different poverty rates, but also affect the entire distribu - [tion of income-to-poverty ratios.](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [These ratios indicate how close](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [someone’s income or resources](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [are to the poverty line by dividing](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [their resources by their poverty](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

## FICA [”‘’](http://www.census.gov/newsroom/blogs/research-matters/2024/09/administrative-data-nonresponse-bias-cps-asec.html)

### Medical expenses [‘”](http://www.census.gov/newsroom/blogs/research-matters/2024/09/administrative-data-nonresponse-bias-cps-asec.html)

[Refundable tax credits include the Earned Income Tax Credit and the refundable portion of the Child Tax Credit.](https://stats.bls.gov/pir/spmhome.htm) [Includes only the refundable portion of the Child Tax Credit.](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) Other noncash benefits include energy and broadband benefits, Special Supplemental Nutrition Program for Women, Infants, and [Children (WIC), and school lunch.](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) Other cash benefits include workers compensation, Temporary Assistance for Needy Families (TANF), and child support received. Note: SNAP is the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program; SSI is Supplemental Security Income; FICA is the Federal Insurance Contributions Act. Population as of March of the following year. More details are available in Table B-7. More information on confidentiality protection, sampling error, nonsampling error, and definitions is available at <[https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf)>. Source: U.S. Census Bureau, Current Population Survey, 2024 Annual Social and Economic Supplement (CPS ASEC).

[B-7) shows how adding or sub](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [-](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [tracting different factors from the](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [resource calculation would affect](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [the number of people in poverty](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [in 2023. Some of the programs in](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) the figure—such as Social Security and unemployment insurance benefits—are included in both the [official poverty measure and the](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [SPM. Others—such as refundable](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) tax credits, SNAP, and school lunch [benefits—are only included in the](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [SPM. Necessary expenses—such](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [as taxes, medical expenses, and](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [work-related expenses—are also](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [deducted from SPM resources but](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) are not considered in the official poverty measure.

To evaluate the effect of programs [that add to resources (e.g., Social](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) Security and cash and noncash transfers), we subtract the value of each component from a unit’s resources and recalculate poverty status. In contrast, to evaluate the effect of expenses, we add back the value of each component to [a unit’s resources. Poverty status](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [changes if subtracting a program](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) benefit decreases an individual’s resources below their poverty threshold or if adding an expense [takes them above their poverty](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [threshold. These additions and](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [subtractions are done indepen](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) - dently and assume no behavioral changes such as shifts in employ - ment status or expenses.

[Removing one item from the](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) calculation of SPM resources and [recalculating poverty rates shows,](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [for example, that Social Security](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) benefits decreased the SPM rate by 8.3 percentage points (Table B-6), lifting 27.6 million people [above the poverty line (Figure 10](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [and Table B-7). Social Security was](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [the largest antipoverty program](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) in 2023, especially for those 65 [years and older. Approximately 70](https://data.census.gov/) percent of the people pulled out of poverty by Social Security (19.5

#### million individuals) fell into that decreased or were not statistically age group. different from 2022.

### [ENDNOTES](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html)

[The Office of Management and Budget](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [(OMB) determined the official definition of](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [poverty in Statistical Poverty Directive 14.](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [Appendix A provides more details on how](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [the Census Bureau calculates official poverty](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) and on the definition of money income. Pretax money income refers to gross income received from a variety of sources like earnings, Social Security, pensions, and disability benefits. It does not include [tax credits, like the Earned Income Tax](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [Credit (EITC) or the Child Tax Credit, nor](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [does it include noncash benefits, such as](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) subsidized housing or nutritional assistance [programs. More information on how income](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [is measured in the official poverty measure is](http://www.census.gov/) [available in Appendix A.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [Gloria Guzman and Melissa Kollar,](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [“Income in the United States: 2023,”](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty.html) Current [Population Reports](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [, P60-282, U.S. Census](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [Bureau, Washington, DC, September 2024,](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) [available at <](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) [www.census.gov/library/](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html >. Katherine Keisler-Starkey and Lisa N. Bunch, “Health Insurance in the United States: 2023,” Current Population Reports , P60-284, U.S. Census Bureau, Washington, DC, [September 2024, available at <](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) [www.census.](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60- 284.html >. [SPM rates for children and those](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [65 years and older were not statistically](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [different in 2023.](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [In 2023, SPM rates were not statistically](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [different for Black and American Indian and](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [Alaska Native individuals, American Indian](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) and Alaska Native and Hispanic individuals, [and Asian individuals and those reporting](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) Two or More Races. # Appendix A. Estimates of Official Poverty

### HOW OFFICIAL POVERTY IS [CALCULATED](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf)

[Following the Office of](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) Management and Budget’s (OMB) Statistical Policy Directive 14, the [U.S. Census Bureau uses a set of](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [dollar value thresholds that vary](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [by family size and composition to](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [determine who is in poverty (avail](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) - [able in the table below).](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

[If a family’s total money income](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [is less than the applicable thresh](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) - old, then that family and every individual in it are considered to be in poverty. The official poverty [thresholds are updated annually for](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) inflation using the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers (CPI-U). The official poverty defini - tion uses money income before taxes or tax credits and excludes capital gains and noncash benefits (such as Supplemental Nutrition [Assistance Program benefits and](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [housing assistance). The thresholds](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) do not vary geographically.

#### [Example: Consider a five-person](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [family with two children, their](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [mother, their father, and their](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html)

### Poverty Thresholds by Size of Family and Number of Related Children Under 18 Years Old: 2023

(In dollars)

[Size of family unit](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html)

| Under 65 years    | . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . |
| ----------------- | ------------------------------------- |
| 65 years and over | . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .       |

| Householder under 65 years    | . . . . . . . |

#### [Weighted Average Thresholds](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

[Since some data users want a sum](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty.html) - [mary of the 48 thresholds to get](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [a general sense of the “poverty](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) line,” the following table provides the weighted average thresholds for 2023. The weighted average [thresholds are based on the relative](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) number of unrelated individuals and primary families of each size and composition and are not used in computing poverty estimates.

### HOW INCOME IS MEASURED

[A family’s money income is used](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [to determine the poverty status](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) of the family and all individuals in it. Money income is calculated for each person 15 years and older [in the Current Population Survey](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [Annual Social and Economic](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [Supplement (CPS ASEC) sample.](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) Respondents are asked questions on the amount of money income received in the preceding calendar

year from each of the following if these people no longer resided sources: in the household at the time of the [interview. [N Not available.](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) ¹ Since 2003, federal surveys have allowed respondents to report more than one race. Therefore, two basic ways of defining a race group are [possible. A group, such as Asian, may be defined as those who reported Asian and no other race (the race-alone or single-race concept) or as](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [those who reported Asian regardless of whether they also reported another race (the race-alone-or-in-combination concept). This table shows](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) data using both approaches. Since Hispanic individuals may be any race, data for the Hispanic population overlap with data for race groups. Of [those who reported only one race in the 2024 CPS ASEC, Hispanic origin was reported by 17.1 percent of White householders, 5.8 percent of](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [Black householders, 2.4 percent of Asian householders, and 32.3 percent of American Indian and Alaska Native householders. Data users should](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [exercise caution when interpreting aggregate results for the Hispanic population or for race groups because these populations consist of many](https://www.nber.org/research/data/us-business-cycle-expansions-and-contractions) distinct groups that differ in socioeconomic characteristics, culture, and nativity. Data on Hispanic origin was first collected in 1972. Data on Asian and Pacific Islander origin and American Indian and Alaska Native origin was first collected in 1987. Estimates for Native Hawaiians and Other Pacific Islanders are not shown separately due to sample size. ² Implementation of 2020 Census-based population controls. [³ Estimates reflect the implementation of an updated processing system and should be used to make comparisons to 2018 and subsequent](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) years. ⁴ The 2014 CPS ASEC included redesigned questions for income and health insurance coverage. All of the approximately 98,000 addresses were eligible to receive the redesigned set of health insurance coverage questions. The redesigned income questions were implemented to a sub - sample of these 98,000 addresses using a probability split panel design. Approximately 68,000 addresses were eligible to receive a set of income questions similar to those used in the 2013 CPS ASEC and the remaining 30,000 addresses were eligible to receive the redesigned income ques - tions. The source of these 2013 estimates is the portion of the CPS ASEC sample that received the redesigned income questions, approximately [30,000 addresses.](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/metro-micro/about/glossary.html) ⁵ The source of these 2013 estimates is the portion of the CPS ASEC sample that received the income questions consistent with the 2013 CPS [ASEC, approximately 68,000 addresses.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) ⁶ Implementation of 2010 Census-based population controls. ⁷ Data have been revised to reflect a correction to the weights in the 2005 CPS ASEC. [⁸ Implementation of a 28,000-household sample expansion.](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [⁹ Implementation of 2000 Census-based population controls.](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) Full implementation of 1990 Census-based sample design and metropolitan definitions, 7,000-household sample reduction, and revised [editing of responses on race.](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [Introduction of 1990 Census-based sample design.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) Data collection method changed from paper and pencil to computer-assisted interviewing. In addition, the 1994 CPS ASEC was revised to allow for the coding of different income amounts on selected questionnaire items. Limits either increased or decreased in the following catego [-](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/technical-documentation/subject-definitions.html) ries: earnings limits increased to $999,999; Social Security limits increased to $49,999; Supplemental Security Income and public assistance limits increased to $24,999; veterans’ benefits limits increased to $99,999; child support and alimony limits decreased to $49,999. Implementation of 1990 Census-based population controls. Estimates are revised to correct for nine omitted weights from the original 1992 CPS ASEC. More information is available in “Money Income of Households, Families, and Persons in the United States: 1992,” P60-184. Estimates reflect the implementation of a new CPS ASEC processing system and are also revised to reflect corrections to the files after publication of the 1988 advance report “Money Income and Poverty Status in the United States: 1988,” P60-166. Full implementation of 1980 Census-based sample design. Implementation of Hispanic population weighting controls and introduction of 1980 Census-based sample design. Implemented three technical changes to the poverty definition. More information is available in “Characteristics of the Population Below the [Poverty Level: 1980,” P60-133.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) Implementation of 1980 Census-based population controls. Questionnaire expanded to show 27 possible values from 51 possible sources of income. Implementation of a new CPS ASEC processing system. Questionnaire expanded to ask 11 income questions. Full implementation of 1970 Census-based sample design. Introduction of 1970 Census-based sample design and population controls. [Implementation of a new CPS ASEC processing system.](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) Note: Details may not sum to totals due to rounding. Estimates may differ from previous publications due to additional rounding implemented [to protect respondent privacy.](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) Source: U.S. Census Bureau, Current Population Survey, 1960 to 2024 Annual Social and Economic Supplements (CPS ASEC).

# Appendix B. The Supplemental Poverty Measure

[The Supplemental Poverty](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [Measure (SPM) was developed](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) following decades of research on poverty measurement. Details regarding the history of the SPM [and the current methodology can](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [be found in the SPM technical](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [documentation at <](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [https://www2.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [census.gov/programs-surveys/](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [supplemental-poverty-measure/](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty.html) >.

### [UPDATES FOR 2023](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html)

#### Updates to Resources

#### Tax Model

SPM estimates for 2023 reflect minor changes to federal, state, and local (for select states) income taxes. Most changes were related to the expiration of state tax credit rebates enacted in 2022. Most expired, but four states extended [or added state tax credit rebates](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [in 2023. Additionally, more than](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [10 states added or expanded their](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [state earned income tax credit,](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [child tax credit, and/or child and](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [dependent care credit programs.](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov)

[Details on the tax model](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) methodology and more information on changes for 2023 [can be found at <](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) [www.census.](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) [gov/topics/income-poverty/](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) income/guidance/tax-model. html [>.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

#### [Interagency Technical Working](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [Group Statement of Duties](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html)

[The ITWG on the SPM meets](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) quarterly to review major and minor methodological changes to the SPM. The ITWG ensures that the SPM captures year-toyear changes in governmental [policy and discusses potential](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [measurement improvements.](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [The ITWG will continue to advise](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [the Census Bureau and BLS on](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [potential changes and updates to](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [the SPM methodology.](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html)

Since 2003, federal surveys have allowed respondents to report more than one race. Therefore, two basic ways of defining a race group are possible. A group, such as Asian, may be A margin of error (MOE) is a measure of an estimate’s variability. The larger the MOE in relation to the size of the estimate, the less reliable the estimate. This number, when added to and Implementation of 2020 Census-based population controls. Estimates reflect the implementation of revised Supplemental Poverty Measure (SPM) methodology. More information is provided in the SPM technical documentation available at [https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [<](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) ⁵ Estimates reflect the implementation of an updated processing system and should be used to make comparisons to 2018 and subsequent years. ⁶ The 2014 CPS ASEC included redesigned questions for income and health insurance coverage. All of the approximately 98,000 addresses were eligible to receive the redesigned set of ⁷ The source of these 2013 estimates is the portion of the CPS ASEC sample that received the income questions consistent with the 2013 CPS ASEC, approximately 68,000 addresses. ⁸ Implementation of 2010 Census-based population controls. Note: Details may not sum to rounding. Estimates may differ from previous publications due to additional rounding implemented to protect respondent privacy. Source: U.S. Census Bureau, Current Population Survey, 2010 to 2024 Annual Social and Economic Supplements (CPS ASEC).

defined as those who reported Asian and no other race (the race-alone or single-race concept) or as those who reported Asian regardless of whether they also reported another race (the race-alone-or-in-combination concept). This table shows data using both approaches. Since Hispanic individuals may be any race, data for the Hispanic population overlap with data for race groups. Of those who reported only one race in the 2024 CPS ASEC, Hispanic origin was reported by 17.1 percent of White householders, 5.8 percent of Black householders, 2.4 percent of Asian householders, and 32.3 percent of American Indian and Alaska Native householders. Data users should exercise caution when interpreting aggregate results for the Hispanic population or for race groups because these populations consist of many distinct groups that differ in socioeconomic characteristics, culture, and nativity. Data on Hispanic origin were first collected in 1972. Data on Asian and Pacific Islander origin and American Indian and Alaska Native origin were first collected in 1987. Estimates for Native Hawaiians and Other Pacific Islanders are not [shown separately due to sample size.](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) subtracted from the estimate, forms the 90 percent confidence interval. MOEs shown in this table are based on standard errors calculated using replicate weights. health insurance coverage questions. The redesigned income questions were implemented to a subsample of these 98,000 addresses using a probability split panel design. Approximately 68,000 addresses were eligible to receive a set of income questions similar to those used in the 2013 CPS ASEC and the remaining 30,000 addresses were eligible to receive the redesigned income questions. The source of these 2013 estimates is the portion of the CPS ASEC sample that received the redesigned income questions, approximately 30,000 addresses.

Z Rounds to zero. * An asterisk preceding an estimate indicates change is statistically different from zero at the 90 percent confidence level. ¹ A margin of error (MOE) is a measure of an estimate’s variability. The larger the MOE in relation to the size of the estimate, the less reliable [the estimate. This number, when added to and subtracted from the estimate, forms the 90 percent confidence interval. MOEs shown in this table](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2023/demo/SEHSD-WP2023-25.html) are based on standard errors calculated using replicate weights. [² Unrelated individuals are people of any age who are not living with any other family members.](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) [³ Federal surveys give respondents the option of reporting more than one race. Therefore, two basic ways of defining a race group are](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) possible. A group, such as Asian, may be defined as those who reported Asian and no other race (the race-alone or single-race concept) or as those who reported Asian regardless of whether they also reported another race (the race-alone-or-in-combination concept). This table shows estimates for the race-alone population and the Two or More Races population. The primary use of the single-race population does not imply that it is the preferred method of presenting or analyzing data. The Census Bureau presents data on race in a variety of ways. Estimates for Native Hawaiians and Other Pacific Islanders are not shown separately due to sample size. ⁴ Information on metropolitan statistical areas and principal cities is available at < [www.census.gov/programs-surveys/metro-micro/about/](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [glossary.html](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [>.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) The sum of those with and without a disability does not equal the total because disability status is not defined for individuals in the [U.S. armed forces.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) Note: SPM is the Supplemental Poverty Measure. Details may not sum to totals due to rounding. Estimates may differ from previous publications due to additional rounding implemented to protect respondent privacy. Source: U.S. Census Bureau, Current Population Survey, 2023 and 2024 Annual Social and Economic Supplements (CPS ASEC).

[* An asterisk preceding an estimate indicates change is statistically different from zero at the 90 percent confidence level.](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2023/demo/SEHSD-WP2023-25.html) [¹ A margin of error (MOE) is a measure of an estimate’s variability. The larger the MOE in relation to the size of the estimate, the less reliable](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) [the estimate. This number, when added to and subtracted from the estimate, forms the 90 percent confidence interval. MOEs shown in this table](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) are based on standard errors calculated using replicate weights. ² Unrelated individuals are people of any age who are not living with any other family members. ³ Federal surveys give respondents the option of reporting more than one race. Therefore, two basic ways of defining a race group are possible. A group, such as Asian, may be defined as those who reported Asian and no other race (the race-alone or single-race concept) or as those who reported Asian regardless of whether they also reported another race (the race-alone-or-in-combination concept). This table shows estimates for the race-alone population and the Two or More Races population. The primary use of the single-race population does not imply that it is the preferred method of presenting or analyzing data. The Census Bureau presents data on race in a variety of ways. Estimates for Native Hawaiians and Other Pacific Islanders are not shown separately due to sample size. ⁴ Information on metropolitan statistical areas and principal cities is available at < [www.census.gov/programs-surveys/metro-micro/about/](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) glossary.html >. The sum of those with and without a disability does not equal the total because disability status is not defined for individuals in the U.S. armed forces.

[¹ A margin of error (MOE) is a measure of an estimate’s variability. The larger the MOE in relation to the size of the estimate, the less reliable](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) [the estimate. This number, when added to and subtracted from the estimate, forms the 90 percent confidence interval. MOEs shown in this table](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) are based on standard errors calculated using replicate weights. [² Federal surveys give respondents the option of reporting more than one race. Therefore, two basic ways of defining a race group are](http://www.census.gov/library/stories/2019/09/us-median-household-income-not-significantly-different-from-2017.html) possible. A group, such as Asian, may be defined as those who reported Asian and no other race (the race-alone or single-race concept) or as those who reported Asian regardless of whether they also reported another race (the race-alone-or-in-combination concept). This table shows estimates for the race-alone population and the Two or More Races population. The primary use of the single-race population does not imply that it is the preferred method of presenting or analyzing data. The Census Bureau presents data on race in a variety of ways. Estimates for Native Hawaiians and Other Pacific Islanders are not shown separately due to sample size.

+

[Note: Official](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) includes unrelated individuals under the age of 15. SPM is the Supplemental Poverty Measure. Details may not sum to totals due to rounding. Estimates may differ from previous publications due to additional rounding implemented to protect respondent privacy. Source: U.S. Census Bureau, Current Population Survey, 2023 and 2024 Annual Social and Economic Supplements (CPS ASEC).

The larger the MOE in relation to the size of the estimate, the less reliable the estimate. This number, when added to and subtracted from the estimate, forms the 90 percent confidence interval. MOEs shown in this table [are based on standard errors calculated using replicate weights.](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) ² Refundable tax credits include the Earned Income Tax Credit (EITC) and the refundable portion of the Child Tax Credit. ³ SNAP is the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program; SSI is Supplemental Security Income; TANF is Temporary Assistance for Needy Families; WIC is the Special Supplemental Nutrition Program for Women, Infants, and Children; FICA is the Federal Insurance Contributions Act. ⁴ Utility assistance includes the Affordable Connectivity Program and other noncash energy benefits. Note: Details may not sum to totals due to rounding. Estimates may differ from previous publications due to additional rounding implemented to protect respondent privacy. # Appendix C. Additional Information

### [SOURCE AND ACCURACY OF](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [THE ESTIMATES](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf)

The Current Population Survey (CPS) is the longest-running [survey conducted by the](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [U.S. Census Bureau. The CPS is a](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [household survey primarily used](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [to collect employment data. The](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [sample universe for the basic CPS](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [consists of the resident civilian](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [noninstitutionalized population](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [of the United States. People in](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) institutions, such as prisons, longterm care hospitals, and nursing homes, are not eligible to be interviewed in the CPS. Students living in dormitories are included in the estimates only if information about them is reported in an interview at their parents’ home. Since the CPS is a household survey, people who are homeless and not living in shelters are not [included in the sample.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf)

The CPS Annual Social and [Economic Supplement (CPS](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [ASEC), the source for the](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [estimates in this report, collects](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [data in February, March, and](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [April each year, asking detailed](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) questions categorizing income into over 50 sources. The key purpose of the survey is to provide timely [and comprehensive estimates](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) [of income, poverty, and health](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) [insurance and to measure change](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [in these national-level estimates.](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) The survey is the official source of national poverty estimates calculated in accordance with the Office of Management [and Budget’s Statistical Policy](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) Directive 14 (Appendix A).

#### The CPS ASEC collects data in [the 50 states and the District](https://data.census.gov/) of Columbia; these data do not

#### [CPS ASEC Modernization](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html)

[The Census Bureau has begun](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [a multiyear effort to modernize](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) many of its surveys, including the CPS. Part of this involves adding an Internet Self-Response (ISR) mode to the CPS and then the CPS ASEC.

[This project requires extensive](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [review and testing to ensure](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [that ISR is a viable collection](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [mode for the CPS ASEC and that](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [changes do not negatively affect](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty.html) [the reliability and comparability](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [of the estimates. The project](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) schedule seeks to align the CPS ASEC modernization effort with that of the CPS to maintain [continuity. However, the schedule](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-284.html) and activities may change to accommodate funding availability, discovery of issues during testing and analysis, and project reprioritization.

For more information about the [ASEC modernization project and](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [timeline, visit the Census Bureau’s](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [CPS ASEC Modernization Efforts](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [webpage at <](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [www.census.gov/](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [programs-surveys/cps/about/](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [modernization/asecmodernization.](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) [html](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) [> or email <](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) [demo.asec.](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) modernization@census.gov >.

#### National Experimental Well-Being [Statistics (NEWS) Project](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html)

[The NEWS project is an](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/income/guidance/tax-model.html) experimental effort to develop [improved estimates of income,](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [poverty, and other measures of](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) economic well-being by using all available survey, administrative, and commercial data.

[The first NEWS release in](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [February 2023 included a working](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) paper that provided improved [estimates of income and official](https://data.census.gov/) poverty statistics for 2018. ### [ACCESSING POVERTY DATA](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html)

#### Additional CPS ASEC Estimates

[Additional estimates from the CPS](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [ASEC are available on the Census](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) Bureau’s poverty websites. This includes detailed and historical tables, press releases, briefings, [and working papers. The websites](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [may be accessed through the](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [Census Bureau’s homepage at](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [<](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [www.census.gov](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/techdocs/cpsmar24.pdf) [> or directly](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [at <](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [www.census.gov/topics/](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [income-poverty/poverty.html](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [> and](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [<](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [www.census.gov/topics/income-](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) [poverty/supplemental-poverty-](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) measure.html >.

#### Public-Use Microdata

#### Public-use CPS ASEC microdata is available for data users of all skill levels.

Data users can create custom statistics from public-use microdata files using the Microdata [Access Tool (MDAT) available at](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [<](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [https://data.census.gov/mdat](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) >.

[Microdata for the 2024 CPS ASEC](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [and earlier years are available](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [online at <](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [www.census.gov/data/](http://www.census.gov/programs-surveys/cps/about/modernization/asecmodernization.html) [datasets/time-series/demo/](http://www.census.gov/data/datasets/time-series/demo/cps/cps-asec.html) [cps/cps-asec.html](mailto:demo.asec.modernization@census.gov) [>. Technical](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) methods have been applied to CPS microdata to avoid disclosing respondents’ identities.

The Census Data Application Programming Interface (API) gives [the public access to raw statistical](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [data from various Census Bureau](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) data programs. It is an efficient way to query data directly from Census Bureau servers. The [historical poverty data found in](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [Table HSTPOV2 are available in the](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/2017/demo/SEHSD-WP2017-42.html) [API at <](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) [www.census.gov/data/](http://www.census.gov/data/developers/data-sets/Poverty-Statistics.html) developers/data-sets/Poverty- Statistics.html [>.](https://data.census.gov/) [The table is also](https://data.census.gov/) available at < [https://data.census.](https://data.census.) gov/ >.

Due to its large sample size, the ACS provides estimates at many levels

#### [Survey of Income and Program](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) [Participation](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html)

[The SIPP provides both monthly](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/poverty/about/history-of-the-poverty-measure.html) and longitudinal data about labor force participation and income sources and amounts at the individual, family, and household levels by following the same [respondents over time. Whereas](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/pam.21833) [the CPS ASEC provides reliable](http://www.census.gov/library/working-papers/1997/demo/fisher-02.html) [estimates of the net change](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [from one year to the next in the](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [overall distribution of economic](https://www2.census.gov/programs-surveys/supplemental-poverty-measure/datasets/spm/spm_techdoc.pdf) [characteristics for the whole](http://www.census.gov/topics/income-poverty/supplemental-poverty-measure.html) [population, it cannot show how](http://www.census.gov/library/publications/2024/demo/p60-282.html) these characteristics change for the same person, family, or household. By collecting monthly data for the same respondents over multiple years, the SIPP makes it possible to observe how economic characteristics
